      <a id="Fedora_Core_6_Starter_Guide" name="Fedora_Core_6_Starter_Guide">
      </a>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Fedora Core 6 Starter Guide
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <b>
        Unofficial Fedora 9 (Sulphur) Starter Guide
       </b>
       
       <a class="external text" href="http://ubuntuguide.org/wiki/Fedora_9" title="http://ubuntuguide.org/wiki/Fedora_9">
        Here!
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       This guide now being maintained by the Linux Center of University of Latvia, and everyone else who is willing to contribute.
      </p>
      <p>
       Contributors:
       <a href="/wiki/User:Orvils" title="User:Orvils">
        orvils
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/User:Fedorajim" title="User:Fedorajim">
        fedorajim
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/User:Mehdi" title="User:Mehdi">
        Mehdi
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/User:Tarcamion" title="User:Tarcamion">
        Tarcamion
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/User:Leslie_Satenstein_Semi-retired_Software_Engineer" title="User:Leslie Satenstein Semi-retired Software Engineer">
        Leslie Satenstein Semi-retired Software Engineer
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/User:Phlo" title="User:Phlo">
        phlo
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other Languages:
       <a class="external text" href="http://ubuntuguide.org/wiki/Fedora_FC6_ro" title="http://ubuntuguide.org/wiki/Fedora_FC6_ro">
        Romanian
       </a>
       in progress
      </p>
      <hr/>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fedora_fc6" title="Fedora fc6">
        Guide for Fedora Core 6 is here!
       </a>
       <br/>
       Much of what's explained in this guide can be done automatically using
       <a href="/wiki/Fedora_frog" title="Fedora frog">
        Fedora Frog
       </a>
      </p>
      <hr/>
      <p>
       <br/>
      </p>

      <a id="General_Notes" name="General_Notes">
      </a>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        General Notes
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        This is an Fedora Core 6 Starter Guide. It is not associated with Fedora and RedHat, inc.
       </li>
       <li>
        Guide is tested on a default "Personal computer" installation of the Fedora Core 6 with default packages.
       </li>
       <li>
        If you see a bluish box, this means you have to execute the commands in Terminal mode (Applications -&gt; System Tools -&gt; Terminal) or use the content of that box as mentioned in some other instructions.
       </li>
       <li>
        To reduce typo mistakes, copy and paste the commands into Terminal mode (right click on the commands -&gt; "Copy" or "Paste". You can also use Ctrl+C to copy and Shift+Insert to paste it)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         Note:
        </b>
        You must run these commands as root. Before you get to do anything you must type
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       su -
      </pre>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        And enter your root password.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         or
        </b>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_get_a_shortcut_to_Root_Terminal" title="">
         #How to get a shortcut to Root Terminal
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        If you don't like working in Terminal mode read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Graphical_User_Interface_for_yum" title="">
         #How to install Graphical User Interface for yum
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        "yum" and "wget" requires Internet connection to install/update/download programs
       </li>
       <li>
        Hope this guide will help you
       </li>
      </ul>

      <a id="Repositories" name="Repositories">
      </a>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Repositories
       </span>
      </h2>
      <a id="How_to_add_extra_repositories" name="How_to_add_extra_repositories">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to add extra repositories
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Replace your old yum.conf with new one
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       cd /etc
mv -f yum.conf yum.conf.bak
wget
       <a class="external free" href="http://www.fedorafaq.org/samples/yum.conf" title="http://www.fedorafaq.org/samples/yum.conf">
        http://www.fedorafaq.org/samples/yum.conf
       </a>
       rpm -Uvh
       <a class="external free" href="http://www.fedorafaq.org/yum" title="http://www.fedorafaq.org/yum">
        http://www.fedorafaq.org/yum
       </a>
      </pre>
      <p>
       <br/>
      </p>
      <a id="Adding_RPMforge_repos" name="Adding_RPMforge_repos">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Adding RPMforge repos
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_GPG_Keys" title="">
         #How to add GPG Keys
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Adding the RPM forge repo is a alternative to the repos that get installed from the
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.fedorafaq.org" title="http://www.fedorafaq.org">
        fedorafaq
       </a>
       website. Note: These two groups are mutually incompatible and can cause errors in your installation if used together for automatic updates.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         freshrpms
        </b>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       rpm -ivh
       <a class="external free" href="http://ftp.freshrpms.net/pub/freshrpms/fedora/linux/6/freshrpms-release/freshrpms-release-1.1-1.fc.noarch.rpm" title="http://ftp.freshrpms.net/pub/freshrpms/fedora/linux/6/freshrpms-release/freshrpms-release-1.1-1.fc.noarch.rpm">
        http://ftp.freshrpms.net/pub/freshrpms/fedora/linux/6/freshrpms-release/freshrpms-release-1.1-1.fc.noarch.rpm
       </a>
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         dries
        </b>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       gedit /etc/yum.repos.d/dries.repo
      </pre>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Add the following lines to the new file
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       [dries]
name=Extra Fedora rpms dries - $releasever - $basearch
baseurl=
       <a class="external free" href="http://ftp.belnet.be/packages/dries.ulyssis.org/fedora/linux/$releasever/$basearch/dries/RPMS/" title="http://ftp.belnet.be/packages/dries.ulyssis.org/fedora/linux/$releasever/$basearch/dries/RPMS/">
        http://ftp.belnet.be/packages/dries.ulyssis.org/fedora/linux/$releasever/$basearch/dries/RPMS/
       </a>
       <a class="external free" href="http://apt.sw.be/dries/fedora/$releasever/$basearch/dries/RPMS/" title="http://apt.sw.be/dries/fedora/$releasever/$basearch/dries/RPMS/">
        http://apt.sw.be/dries/fedora/$releasever/$basearch/dries/RPMS/
       </a>
       failovermethod=priority
enabled=0
gpgcheck=1
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         newrpms
        </b>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       gedit /etc/yum.repos.d/newrpms.repo
      </pre>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Add the following lines to the new file
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       [newrpms.sunsite.dk]
name=Fedora Core 5 i386 NewRPMS.sunsite.dk
baseurl=
       <a class="external free" href="http://newrpms.sunsite.dk/apt/redhat/en/$basearch/fc$releasever" title="http://newrpms.sunsite.dk/apt/redhat/en/$basearch/fc$releasever">
        http://newrpms.sunsite.dk/apt/redhat/en/$basearch/fc$releasever
       </a>
       <a class="external free" href="http://newrpms.atrpms.net/apt/redhat/en/$basearch/fc$releasever" title="http://newrpms.atrpms.net/apt/redhat/en/$basearch/fc$releasever">
        http://newrpms.atrpms.net/apt/redhat/en/$basearch/fc$releasever
       </a>
       failovermethod=priority
enabled=0
gpgcheck=1
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_import_GPG_Keys" name="How_to_import_GPG_Keys">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to import GPG Keys
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Remember you have to do this as root Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       rpm --import
       <a class="external free" href="http://freshrpms.net/packages/RPM-GPG-KEY.txt" title="http://freshrpms.net/packages/RPM-GPG-KEY.txt">
        http://freshrpms.net/packages/RPM-GPG-KEY.txt
       </a>
       rpm --import
       <a class="external free" href="http://dries.ulyssis.org/rpm/RPM-GPG-KEY.dries.txt" title="http://dries.ulyssis.org/rpm/RPM-GPG-KEY.dries.txt">
        http://dries.ulyssis.org/rpm/RPM-GPG-KEY.dries.txt
       </a>
       rpm --import
       <a class="external free" href="http://newrpms.sunsite.dk/gpg-pubkey-newrpms.txt" title="http://newrpms.sunsite.dk/gpg-pubkey-newrpms.txt">
        http://newrpms.sunsite.dk/gpg-pubkey-newrpms.txt
       </a>
       rpm --import /usr/share/doc/fedora-release-*/*GPG-KEY*
      </pre>
      <a id="Fedora_Updates" name="Fedora_Updates">
      </a>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Fedora Updates
       </span>
      </h2>
      <a id="How_to_manually_update_Fedora" name="How_to_manually_update_Fedora">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to manually update Fedora
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum check-update
yum update
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Alternative is to use pup (Package Updater)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       pup
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        From the menu
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Applications -&gt; System Tools -&gt; Software Updater
      </p>
      <a id="Add-On_Applications" name="Add-On_Applications">
      </a>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Add-On Applications
       </span>
      </h2>
      <a id="How_To_use_Yum" name="How_To_use_Yum">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How To use Yum
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Yum is a very powerfull package manager. yum will resolve dependencies for you and makes installing applications a breeze. yum also searches, removes, and lists packages for you.
      </p>
      <pre>
       usage: yum [options] &lt; update | install | info | remove | list |
clean | provides | search | check-update | groupinstall |
groupupdate | grouplist | groupinfo | groupremove |
makecache | localinstall | erase | upgrade | whatprovides |
localupdate | resolvedep | shell | deplist &gt;
options:
-h, --help            show this help message and exit
-t, --tolerant        be tolerant of errors
-C                    run entirely from cache, don't update cache
-c  [config file]     config file location
-R  [minutes]         maximum command wait time
-d  [debug level]     debugging output level
-e  [error level]     error output level
-y                    answer yes for all questions
--version             show Yum version and exit
--installroot=[path]  set install root
--enablerepo=[repo]   enable one or more repositories (wildcards allowed)
--disablerepo=[repo]  disable one or more repositories (wildcards allowed)
--exclude=[package]   exclude package(s) by name or glob
--obsoletes           enable obsoletes processing during updates
--noplugins           disable Yum plugins
      </pre>
      <p>
       From a first look this can look rather intimidating, but this is rather easy.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         Examples:
        </b>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To seach for a application
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Yum will search all your enabled repos and tell you where you can obtain the package from
      </p>
      <pre>
       yum search application_name
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Yum can list all available packages from your enabled repos and tell you where you can obtain the package from:
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum list available
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To find out more info about some package
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum info application_name
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Installing applications
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Inastalling is as easy as
      </p>
      <pre>
       yum install application_name
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Listing rpms
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       yum can list installed rpms for you from the repos  you have enabled
      </p>
      <pre>
       yum list extras
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Removing rpms
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Yum can remove a application and the dependenciesit installed with tat application. it will not remove depenencies if another application installed needs them.
      </p>
      <pre>
       yum remove application_name
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Updating the system
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Yum can update the system for you with out user interact if you want it to.
      </p>
      <pre>
       yum update
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Not sure if you have upates?
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum check-update
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Local install
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       downloaded a rpm and cannot install it with rpm because of dependencies?
      </p>
      <pre>
       yum localinstall /path/to/the/rpm
      </pre>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Happy yumming...
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       <br/>
       Incase you are using yum from behind a http proxy server then just open /etc/yum.conf by using
      </p>
      <p>
       vi /etc/yum.conf
      </p>
      <p>
       and add the following line
      </p>
      <p>
       proxy=
       <a class="external free" href="http://username:password@your-servers-ip-address:portnumber" title="http://username:password@your-servers-ip-address:portnumber">
        http://username:password@your-servers-ip-address:portnumber
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       where username is your username and password is your accounts password,your-servers-ip-address is the IP of your server and port number is the port through which you access your proxy server
      </p>
      <p>
       note: please make sure that you are logged in as root while making these changes...
      </p>
      <p>
       --
       <a class="new" href="/index.php?title=User:Manumehrotra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="User:Manumehrotra (page does not exist)">
        Manumehrotra
       </a>
       06:05, 25 December 2007 (EET)
      </p>
      <a id="How_to_install_Graphical_User_Interface_for_yum" name="How_to_install_Graphical_User_Interface_for_yum">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install Graphical User Interface for yum
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum -y install yumex
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Applications -&gt; System Tools -&gt; Yum Extender
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="NetworkManager_for_Gnome" name="NetworkManager_for_Gnome">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        NetworkManager for Gnome
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Start the services
      </p>
      <pre>
       /sbin/chkconfig --level 345 NetworkManager on
/sbin/chkconfig --level 345 NetworkManagerDispatcher on
service NetworkManager start
service NetworkManagerDispatcher start
      </pre>
      <p>
       <br/>
       Click the Radar or connected icon in the system tray and choose "New wireless network". 
Enter your information
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.fedorajim.homelinux.com/samples/NetworkManagerConnected.png" title="http://www.fedorajim.homelinux.com/samples/NetworkManagerConnected.png">
        Screenshot
       </a>
      </p>
      <a id="How_to_install_Menu_Editor_for_GNOME" name="How_to_install_Menu_Editor_for_GNOME">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install Menu Editor for GNOME

      </h4>

         #General Notes

       yum -y install alacarte
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>

      <a id="How_to_install_Clipboard_Daemon_for_GNOME" name="How_to_install_Clipboard_Daemon_for_GNOME">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install Clipboard Daemon for GNOME
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        first 5 commands are done as root the last is user your user ID.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       wget -c
       <a class="external free" href="http://easylinux.info/uploads/gnome-clipboard-daemon-1.0.bin.tar.bz2" title="http://easylinux.info/uploads/gnome-clipboard-daemon-1.0.bin.tar.bz2">
        http://easylinux.info/uploads/gnome-clipboard-daemon-1.0.bin.tar.bz2
       </a>
       tar jxvf gnome-clipboard-daemon-1.0.bin.tar.bz2 -C /usr/bin/
rm -f gnome-clipboard-daemon-1.0.bin.tar.bz2
chown root:root /usr/bin/gnome-clipboard-daemon
chmod 755 /usr/bin/gnome-clipboard-daemon
gnome-clipboard-daemon &amp;
exit
export EDITOR=gedit &amp;&amp; crontab -e
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Add the following line at the end of file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       @reboot gnome-clipboard-daemon
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_install_Java_with_Plug-in_for_Mozilla_Firefox" name="How_to_install_Java_with_Plug-in_for_Mozilla_Firefox">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install Java with Plug-in for Mozilla Firefox
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Download Linux self-extracting file (jre-1_5_0_10-linux-i586.bin) from
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       <a class="external text" href="http://java.com/en/download/manual.jsp" title="http://java.com/en/download/manual.jsp">
        Java's Site
       </a>
       and save it to your home folder
      </p>
      <pre>
       mv jre-1_5_0_10-linux-i586.bin /opt
cd /opt
chmod +x jre-1_5_0_10-linux-i586.bin
./jre-1_5_0_10-linux-i586.bin
 ln -s /opt/jre1.5.0_10/plugin/i386/ns7/libjavaplugin_oji.so /usr/lib/mozilla/plugins/libjavaplugin_oji.so
      </pre>
      <p>
       The Java plugin is now installed  Confirm with the command below that the sym links are green
      </p>
      <pre>
       ls /usr/lib/mozilla/plugins
      </pre>
      <p>
       <br/>
       To run Java enabled applications like limewire continue below
      </p>
      <pre>
       gedit /etc/profile.d/java.sh
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines to the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       #!/bin/sh
JAVA_HOME=/opt/jre1.5.0_10
export JAVA_HOME
JAVA_BIN=$JAVA_HOME/bin
CLASSPATH=$CLASSPATH:$JAVA_HOME:$JAVA_HOME/lib
PATH=$JAVA_BIN:$PATH
export JAVA_BIN CLASSPATH PATH
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       source /etc/profile.d/java.sh
/usr/sbin/alternatives --install /usr/bin/java java /opt/jre1.5.0_10/bin/java 2
/usr/sbin/alternatives --config java
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        You will see the following screen
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       There are 2 programs which provide 'java'.

  Selection    Command
-----------------------------------------------

*+ 1           /usr/lib/jvm/jre-1.4.2-gcj/bin/java
   2           /opt/jre1.5.0_10/bin/java

Enter to keep the current selection[+], or type selection number:
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Enter
        <b>
         2
        </b>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.java.com/en/download/help/testvm.xml" title="http://www.java.com/en/download/help/testvm.xml">
         Test your Java
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_install_Flash_Player_.28Macromedia_Flash.29_Plug-in_for_Mozilla_Firefox" name="How_to_install_Flash_Player_.28Macromedia_Flash.29_Plug-in_for_Mozilla_Firefox">

      <a id="How_to_install_PDF_Reader_.28Adobe_Reader.29" name="How_to_install_PDF_Reader_.28Adobe_Reader.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install PDF Reader (Adobe Reader)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        You can already view .pdf documents, but if you wish to have Adobe Reader
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       wget -c
       <a class="external free" href="http://ardownload.adobe.com/pub/adobe/reader/unix/7x/7.0.5/enu/AdobeReader_enu-7.0.5-1.i386.rpm" title="http://ardownload.adobe.com/pub/adobe/reader/unix/7x/7.0.5/enu/AdobeReader_enu-7.0.5-1.i386.rpm">
        http://ardownload.adobe.com/pub/adobe/reader/unix/7x/7.0.5/enu/AdobeReader_enu-7.0.5-1.i386.rpm
       </a>
       yum -y install compat-libstdc++-33
rpm -i AdobeReader_enu-7.0.5-1.i386.rpm
rm -f AdobeReader_enu-7.0.5-1.i386.rpm
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Applications -&gt; Office -&gt; Adobe Reader
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="Link_Adobe_Acrobat_to_the_mozilla_plugins" name="Link_Adobe_Acrobat_to_the_mozilla_plugins">

      </pre>

      <a id="How_to_install_File_share_utility_.28DC.2B.2B.29" name="How_to_install_File_share_utility_.28DC.2B.2B.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install File share utility (DC++)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The following is a precompiled package. Information on how to get the latest version of linuxdcpp from the official cvs
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.my-guides.net/en/content/view/59/26/1/2/#linuxdcpp" title="http://www.my-guides.net/en/content/view/59/26/1/2/#linuxdcpp">
        here
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       wget -c
       <a class="external free" href="http://easylinux.info/uploads/linuxdcpp.tar.gz" title="http://easylinux.info/uploads/linuxdcpp.tar.gz">
        http://easylinux.info/uploads/linuxdcpp.tar.gz
       </a>
       tar zxvf linuxdcpp.tar.gz -C /opt
rm -f linuxdcpp.tar.gz
gedit /usr/share/applications/dcpp.desktop
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines into the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       [Desktop Entry]
Encoding=UTF-8
Name=LinuxDC++
Exec=linuxdcpp
Terminal=false
Type=Application
StartupNotify=true
Icon=/opt/linuxdcpp/pixmaps/linuxdcpp.png
Categories=Application;Network;
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Applications -&gt; Internet -&gt; DC++
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_install_P2P_BitTorrent_Client_.28Azureus.29" name="How_to_install_P2P_BitTorrent_Client_.28Azureus.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install P2P BitTorrent Client (Azureus)
       </span>
      </h4>

        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       wget -c
       <a class="external free" href="http://heanet.dl.sourceforge.net/sourceforge/azureus/Azureus_2.3.0.6_linux.tar.bz2" title="http://heanet.dl.sourceforge.net/sourceforge/azureus/Azureus_2.3.0.6_linux.tar.bz2">
        http://heanet.dl.sourceforge.net/sourceforge/azureus/Azureus_2.3.0.6_linux.tar.bz2
       </a>

      </pre>

Comment=A Bittorrent client
Exec=/opt/azureus/azureus
Icon=/opt/azureus/Azureus.png
Terminal=false
Type=Application
Categories=Application;Network;
      </pre>
      <ul>

       </li>

      <a id="How_to_install_P2P_Gnutella_Client_.28LimeWire.29" name="How_to_install_P2P_Gnutella_Client_.28LimeWire.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install P2P Gnutella Client (LimeWire)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_J2SE_Runtime_Environment_.28JRE.29_with_Plug-in_for_Mozilla_Firefox" title="">
         #How to install J2SE Runtime Environment (JRE) with Plug-in for Mozilla Firefox
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       wget -c
       <a class="external free" href="http://easylinux.info/uploads/LimeWireOther.zip" title="http://easylinux.info/uploads/LimeWireOther.zip">
        http://easylinux.info/uploads/LimeWireOther.zip
       </a>
       unzip -u LimeWireOther.zip -d /opt/
rm -f LimeWireOther.zip
gedit /usr/bin/runLime.sh
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines into the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       cd /opt/LimeWire/
./runLime.sh
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       chmod +x /usr/bin/runLime.sh
gedit /usr/share/applications/LimeWire.desktop
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines into the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       [Desktop Entry]
Name=LimeWire
Comment=LimeWire
Exec=runLime.sh
Icon=/opt/LimeWire/LimeWire.ico
Terminal=false
Type=Application
Categories=Application;Network;
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Applications -&gt; Internet -&gt; LimeWire
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_install_Messenger_.28Skype.29" name="How_to_install_Messenger_.28Skype.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install Messenger (Skype)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       wget -c
       <a class="external free" href="http://download.skype.com/linux/skype_staticQT-1.2.0.18.tar.bz2" title="http://download.skype.com/linux/skype_staticQT-1.2.0.18.tar.bz2">
        http://download.skype.com/linux/skype_staticQT-1.2.0.18.tar.bz2
       </a>
       tar jxvf skype_staticQT-1.2.0.18.tar.bz2 -C /opt/
ln -s /opt/skype-1.2.0.18/skype /usr/bin/skype
cp /opt/skype-1.2.0.18/skype.desktop /usr/share/applications/skype.desktop
cp /opt/skype-1.2.0.18/icons/skype_32_32.png /usr/share/pixmaps/skype.png
rm -f skype_staticQT-1.2.0.18.tar.bz2
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Applications -&gt; Internet -&gt; Skype
       </li>
      </ul>

      <a id="How_to_install_Multimedia_Player_.28RealPlayer_10.29" name="How_to_install_Multimedia_Player_.28RealPlayer_10.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install Multimedia Player (RealPlayer 10)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum -y install compat-libstdc++-33
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Download RealPlayer Gold from
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.real.com/realcom/R?href=http%3A%2F%2Fforms.real.com%2Freal%2Fplayer%2Fdownload.html%3Ff%3Dunix%2FRealPlayer10GOLD.rpm%26product%3Dplayerplus%26system%3Dlinux&amp;pageid=linuxPage&amp;pageregion=advanced_install&amp;src=linux&amp;pcode=rn&amp;opage=linux" title="http://www.real.com/realcom/R?href=http%3A%2F%2Fforms.real.com%2Freal%2Fplayer%2Fdownload.html%3Ff%3Dunix%2FRealPlayer10GOLD.rpm%26product%3Dplayerplus%26system%3Dlinux&amp;pageid=linuxPage&amp;pageregion=advanced_install&amp;src=linux&amp;pcode=rn&amp;opage=linux">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Install it.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Assumed that .rpm file has been downloaded to your Desktop, because Firefox by default downloads everything to your Desktop
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       rpm -ivh Desktop/RealPlayer10GOLD.rpm
yum remove HelixPlayer
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Applications -&gt; Sound &amp; Video -&gt; RealPlayer 10
       </li>
      </ul>

      <a id="How_to_install_K9copy" name="How_to_install_K9copy">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install K9copy
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Multimedia_Codecs" title="">
         #How to install Multimedia Codecs
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_DVD_playback_capability" title="">
         #How to install DVD playback capability
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Multimedia_Player_.28MPlayer.29_with_Plug-in_for_Mozilla_Firefox" title="">
         #How to install Multimedia Player (MPlayer) with Plug-in for Mozilla Firefox
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Menu_Editor_for_GNOME" title="">
         #How to install Menu Editor for GNOME
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       K9copy is the linux version of DVDshrink for windows.  Since K9copy is  a KDE application there may not be  a menu opton for it in Gnome.  See the above link for menu editing
      </p>
      <pre>
       wget
       <a class="external free" href="http://www.fedoraserver.org/files/k9/K9copy-1.0.4_LP-2-1.i386.rpm" title="http://www.fedoraserver.org/files/k9/K9copy-1.0.4_LP-2-1.i386.rpm">
        http://www.fedoraserver.org/files/k9/K9copy-1.0.4_LP-2-1.i386.rpm
       </a>
       yum -y --enablerepo=freshrpms install libdvdread libdvdread-devel
rpm -ivh K9copy-1.0.4_LP-2-1.i386.rpm
      </pre>
      <p>
       <br/>
      </p>
      <a id="How_to_install_DVD_Ripper_.28dvd::rip.29" name="How_to_install_DVD_Ripper_.28dvd::rip.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install DVD Ripper (dvd::rip)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Multimedia_Codecs" title="">
         #How to install Multimedia Codecs
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_DVD_playback_capability" title="">
         #How to install DVD playback capability
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Multimedia_Player_.28MPlayer.29_with_Plug-in_for_Mozilla_Firefox" title="">
         #How to install Multimedia Player (MPlayer) with Plug-in for Mozilla Firefox
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_RAR_Archiver_.28rar.29" title="">
         #How to install RAR Archiver (rar)
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum -y install dvdrip
yum --enablerepo=freshrpms install vcdimager
yum -y install cdrdao
yum --enablerepo=freshrpms install subtitleripper
ln -fs /usr/bin/rar /usr/bin/rar-2.80
gedit /usr/share/applications/dvdrip.desktop
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines into the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       [Desktop Entry]
Name=dvd::rip 
Comment=dvd::rip
Exec=dvdrip
Icon=/usr/share/perl5/Video/DVDRip/icon.xpm
Terminal=false
Type=Application
Categories=Application;AudioVideo;
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Applications -&gt; Sound &amp; Video -&gt; dvd::rip
       </li>
      </ul>

      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install RSS/RDF/Atom Newsreader (RSSOwl)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_J2SE_Runtime_Environment_.28JRE.29_with_Plug-in_for_Mozilla_Firefox" title="">
         #How to install J2SE Runtime Environment (JRE) with Plug-in for Mozilla Firefox
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       wget -c
       <a class="external free" href="http://easylinux.info/uploads/rssowl_linux_1_1_3_bin.tar.gz" title="http://easylinux.info/uploads/rssowl_linux_1_1_3_bin.tar.gz">
        http://easylinux.info/uploads/rssowl_linux_1_1_3_bin.tar.gz
       </a>
       tar zxvf rssowl_linux_1_1_3_bin.tar.gz -C /opt/
chown -R root:root /opt/rssowl_linux_1_1_3_bin/
gedit /usr/bin/runRSSOwl.sh
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines into the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       export MOZILLA_FIVE_HOME=/usr/lib/mozilla-firefox
export LD_LIBRARY_PATH=$LD_LIBRARY_PATH:${MOZILLA_FIVE_HOME}:${LD_LIBRARY_PATH}
cd /opt/rssowl_linux_1_1_3_bin/
./run.sh
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       chmod +x /usr/bin/runRSSOwl.sh
gedit /usr/share/applications/RSSOwl.desktop
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines into the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       [Desktop Entry]
Name=RSSOwl
Comment=RSSOwl
Exec=runRSSOwl.sh
Icon=/opt/rssowl_linux_1_1_3_bin/rssowl.xpm
Terminal=false
Type=Application
Categories=Application;Network;
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Applications -&gt; Internet -&gt; RSSOwl
       </li>
      </ul>

      <a id="How_to_set_up_Development_environment" name="How_to_set_up_Development_environment">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to set up Development environment
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Add development repo
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       gedit /etc/yum.repos.d/fedora-devel.repo
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Add the following lines to the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       [development]
name=Fedora Core $releasever - Development Tree
#baseurl=
       <a class="external free" href="http://download.fedora.redhat.com/pub/fedora/linux/core/development/$basearch/" title="http://download.fedora.redhat.com/pub/fedora/linux/core/development/$basearch/">
        http://download.fedora.redhat.com/pub/fedora/linux/core/development/$basearch/
       </a>
       mirrorlist=
       <a class="external free" href="http://fedora.redhat.com/download/mirrors/fedora-core-rawhide" title="http://fedora.redhat.com/download/mirrors/fedora-core-rawhide">
        http://fedora.redhat.com/download/mirrors/fedora-core-rawhide
       </a>
       enabled=1
gpgcheck=0
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum groupinstall "Development Tools"
      </pre>

      <h2>

      </h2>
      <a id="How_to_install_KDE" name="How_to_install_KDE">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install KDE
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        You may also look at some
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.kde.org/screenshots/" title="http://www.kde.org/screenshots/">
         KDE Screenshots
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Use
        <i>
         Desktop -&gt; System Settings -&gt; Add/Remove Applications
        </i>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         or
        </b>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       yum -y groupinstall KDE
      </pre>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         or
        </b>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       yum -y install htdig
yum -y install kdebase
yum -y install arts
yum -y install desktop-printing
yum -y install kdegraphics
yum -y install kdenetwork
yum -y install kdemultimedia
yum -y install kdeaddons
yum -y install kdeutils
yum -y install kdeartwork
yum -y install autorun
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Log out
       </li>
       <li>
        In Sessions choose
        <b>
         KDE
        </b>
       </li>
       <li>
        Log in
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_install_XFCE" name="How_to_install_XFCE">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install XFCE
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        You may also look at some
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.xfce.org/about/screenshots" title="http://www.xfce.org/about/screenshots">
         XFCE Screenshots
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         or
        </b>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       yum -y groupinstall XFCE
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Log out
       </li>
       <li>
        In Sessions choose
        <b>
         XFCE
        </b>
       </li>
       <li>
        Log in
       </li>
      </ul>

      <a id="Hardware" name="Hardware">
      </a>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Hardware
       </span>
      </h2>
      <a id="Activate_side-mouse-buttons_in_FireFox" name="Activate_side-mouse-buttons_in_FireFox">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Activate side-mouse-buttons in FireFox
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Just add two lines to xorg.conf will activate side-mouse-buttons in FireFox.  This should work with most 5-button mouse.  Here is a list of mice that worked with this instruction.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Logitech MX510
       </li>
       <li>
        Logitech MX518
       </li>
       <li>
        Logitech MX700
       </li>
       <li>
        Intellimouse Explorer (first edition)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Backup Gnome configuration file
      </p>
      <pre>
       sudo cp /etc/X11/xorg.conf /etc/X11/xorg.conf.bak
      </pre>
      <p>
       Modify the Gnome configuration file
      </p>
      <pre>
       gksudo gedit /etc/X11/xorg.conf
      </pre>
      <p>
       Find the Input Device section for your mouse and add two lines as shown below.  You may also increase the number of buttons if your mouse has more than 7, just fix the rest of the section based upon the number of buttons (remember back/forward, wheel click &amp; tilt left/right all count as buttons)
      </p>
      <p>
       Change:
      </p>
      <pre>
       Section "InputDevice"
	Identifier "Configured Mouse"
	Driver "mouse"
	Option "CorePointer"
	...
	Option "Protocol" "ExplorerPS/2"
	...
	Option "Emulate3Buttons"       "true"
EndSection
      </pre>
      <p>
       to:
      </p>
      <pre>
       Section "InputDevice"
	Identifier "Configured Mouse"
	Driver "mouse"
	Option "CorePointer"
	...
	Option "Protocol" "ExplorerPS/2"
	...
	Option "Emulate3Buttons"       "true"
	Option "Buttons" "7"
 	Option "ButtonMapping" "1 2 3 6 7"
EndSection
      </pre>
      <p>
       At this point you can reboot your computer or reboot Gnome (Ctrl-Alt-BackSpace) to see if your forward/back buttons work in FireFox.  They still won't work in Nautilus yet until you install the imwheel dameon.
      </p>
      <a id="how_to_get_wireless_working_Intel_IPW2200_b.2Cg" name="how_to_get_wireless_working_Intel_IPW2200_b.2Cg">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        how to get wireless working Intel IPW2200 b,g
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       download
       <a class="external autonumber" href="http://ipw2200.sourceforge.net/firmware.php?fid=6" title="http://ipw2200.sourceforge.net/firmware.php?fid=6">
        [1]
       </a>
       Agree to the licence and save the file to your desktop then open the terminal and copy &amp; paste each line.
      </p>
      <pre>
       mkdir tmp
mv ~/Desktop/*-2.4.tgz ~/tmp 
cd tmp
tar -zxvf ipw2200-fw-2.4.tgz
cp * /lib/firmware
rmmod ipw2200
modprobe ipw2200
iwconfig
      </pre>
      <p>
       you should now see a access point
You can use NetworkManager to control your wireless actvity
      </p>
      <pre>
       <a href="#NetworkManager_for_Gnome" title="">
        #NetworkManager_for_Gnome
       </a>
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_install_Graphics_Driver_.28NVIDIA.29" name="How_to_install_Graphics_Driver_.28NVIDIA.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install Graphics Driver (NVIDIA)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum -y install nvidia-glx kernel-module-nvidia-$(uname -r)
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_restart_GNOME_without_rebooting_computer" title="">
         #How to restart GNOME without rebooting computer
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        If you have any problems see
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.nvnews.net/vbulletin/forumdisplay.php?s=&amp;forumid=14" title="http://www.nvnews.net/vbulletin/forumdisplay.php?s=&amp;forumid=14">
         nV News "Linux and nVidia Graphics" forum
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <b>
         or
        </b>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        See
        <a class="external free" href="http://www.mjmwired.net/resources/mjm-fedora-fc5.html#nvidia" title="http://www.mjmwired.net/resources/mjm-fedora-fc5.html#nvidia">
         http://www.mjmwired.net/resources/mjm-fedora-fc5.html#nvidia
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_install_Graphics_Driver_.28ATI.29" name="How_to_install_Graphics_Driver_.28ATI.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install Graphics Driver (ATI)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum -y install ati-fglrx kernel-module-fglrx-$(uname -r)
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        If you have an Intel motherboard, you will have to modify your xorg.conf file after installing the drivers:
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       gedit /etc/X11/xorg.conf
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Find the following line
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       Driver "fglrx"
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Add the following line below it
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       Option "UseInternalAGPGART" "no"
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Some users may experience problems with certain FIREGL cards (in my case an ibm t43p laptop with a v3200 ati firegl) whereby projects such as cedega and wine refuse to work with 3d graphics, but native binaries work fine. A possible workaround is to add the following line after those mentioned above
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       Option "UseFastTLS" "2"
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        This option used to be configured with the older ati drivers when you ran "fglrxconfig". I have not yet found a way to get it to appear with "aticonfig", hence the manual insertion. This option is good for several linux distros I have tried, fedora core 5, ubuntu dapper and suse 10.1
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_identify_Modem_chipset" name="How_to_identify_Modem_chipset">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to identify Modem chipset
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        To install Modem chipset identifier
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Basic_Compilers_.28build-essential.29" title="">
         #How to install Basic Compilers (build-essential)
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       wget -c
       <a class="external free" href="http://easylinux.info/uploads/scanModem.gz" title="http://easylinux.info/uploads/scanModem.gz">
        http://easylinux.info/uploads/scanModem.gz
       </a>
       gunzip -c scanModem.gz &gt; scanModem
chmod +x scanModem
cp scanModem /usr/bin/
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To identify Modem chipset
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       scanModem
gedit Modem/ModemData.txt
      </pre>

      <a id="How_to_speed_up_CD.2FDVD-ROM" name="How_to_speed_up_CD.2FDVD-ROM">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to speed up CD/DVD-ROM
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that /dev/cdrom is the location of CD/DVD-ROM
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       /sbin/hdparm -d1 /dev/cdrom
gedit /etc/hdparm.conf
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines in the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       /dev/cdrom {
    dma = on
}
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_mount.2Funmount_CD.2FDVD-ROM_manually.2C_and_show_all_hidden_and_associated_files.2Ffolders" name="How_to_mount.2Funmount_CD.2FDVD-ROM_manually.2C_and_show_all_hidden_and_associated_files.2Ffolders">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to mount/unmount CD/DVD-ROM manually, and show all hidden and associated files/folders
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that /media/cdrom0/ is the location of CD/DVD-ROM
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To mount CD/DVD-ROM
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       mount /media/cdrom0/ -o unhide
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To unmount CD/DVD-ROM
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       umount /media/cdrom0/
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_forcefully_unmount_CD.2FDVD-ROM_manually" name="How_to_forcefully_unmount_CD.2FDVD-ROM_manually">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to forcefully unmount CD/DVD-ROM manually
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that /media/cdrom0/ is the location of CD/DVD-ROM
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       umount /media/cdrom0/ -l
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_remount_.2Fetc.2Ffstab_without_rebooting" name="How_to_remount_.2Fetc.2Ffstab_without_rebooting">

      <a id="CD.2FDVD_Burning" name="CD.2FDVD_Burning">
      </a>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        CD/DVD Burning
       </span>
      </h2>
      <a id="How_to_blank_CD-RW.2FDVD-RW" name="How_to_blank_CD-RW.2FDVD-RW">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to blank CD-RW/DVD-RW
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that /dev/cdrom is the location of CD/DVD-ROM
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       umount /dev/cdrom
cdrecord dev=/dev/cdrom blank=fast
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_burn_files.2Ffolders_into_CD.2FDVD" name="How_to_burn_files.2Ffolders_into_CD.2FDVD">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to burn files/folders into CD/DVD
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       nautilus burn:///
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        File Browser: CD/DVD Creator
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Drag files/folders into window
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       File Menu -&gt; Write to Disc... -&gt; Write
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_burn_Image_.28ISO.29_files_into_CD.2FDVD" name="How_to_burn_Image_.28ISO.29_files_into_CD.2FDVD">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to burn Image (ISO) files into CD/DVD
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       Right click on Image (ISO) file -&gt; Write to Disc... -&gt; Write
      </pre>

      <a id="How_to_create_Image_.28ISO.29_files_from_CD.2FDVD" name="How_to_create_Image_.28ISO.29_files_from_CD.2FDVD">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to create Image (ISO) files from CD/DVD
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that /dev/cdrom is the location of CD/DVD-ROM
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       umount /dev/cdrom
dd if=/dev/cdrom of=file.iso bs=1024
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_create_Image_.28ISO.29_files_from_folders" name="How_to_create_Image_.28ISO.29_files_from_folders">

      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       mkisofs -o file.iso /location_of_folder/
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_generate_MD5_checksum_files" name="How_to_generate_MD5_checksum_files">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to generate MD5 checksum files
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       md5sum file.iso &gt; file.iso.md5
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_check_MD5_checksum_of_files" name="How_to_check_MD5_checksum_of_files">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to check MD5 checksum of files
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that file.iso and file.iso.md5 are in the same folder
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       md5sum -c file.iso.md5
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_mount.2Funmount_Image_.28ISO.29_files_without_burning" name="How_to_mount.2Funmount_Image_.28ISO.29_files_without_burning">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to mount/unmount Image (ISO) files without burning
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        To mount Image (ISO) file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       mkdir /media/iso
modprobe loop
mount file.iso /media/iso/ -t iso9660 -o loop
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To unmount Image (ISO) file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       umount /media/iso/
      </pre>

      <a id="Networking" name="Networking">
      </a>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Networking
       </span>
      </h2>
      <a id="How_to_configure_VPN_client_.28PPTP.29" name="How_to_configure_VPN_client_.28PPTP.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to configure VPN client (PPTP)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Install PPTP Config
      </p>
      <pre>
       rpm -Uvh http://pptpclient.sourceforge.net/yum/stable/fc5/pptp-release-current.noarch.rpm
yum --enablerepo=pptp-stable install pptpconfig
      </pre>
      <a id="Configure_PPTP_Config" name="Configure_PPTP_Config">
      </a>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Configure PPTP Config
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       Launch it beneath Internet, then input the following fields as described:
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        Server Tab
       </i>
       :
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Name - short description of this connection
       </li>
       <li>
        Server - dns server name or ip address of the target PPTP server
       </li>
       <li>
        Domain - domain name if using Windows or Active Directory authentication
       </li>
       <li>
        Username - simply your username to login with
       </li>
       <li>
        Password - the password to use with the username above
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       <i>
        Routing Tab
       </i>
       : For Routing Style select 'Client to LAN'.  Then click Edit Network Routes then add the target network in the following format "192.168.0.0/24' for all IP Addresses in the block 192.168.0.*.  Next  type a short name for this network route and click Add.
      </p>
      <p>
       <br/>
       <i>
        DNS Tab
       </i>
       : Checking Automatic is recommended, if this doesn't work however you can specify DNS Servers in the Server box.  Also input something like "search mycompany.com" in the Options field which will make host name resolution simpler.
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        Encryption &amp; Misc Tab
       </i>
       : Defaults here should be good, but if you are troubleshooting you can uncheck everything.
      </p>
      <p>
       Finally click Add then Start
      </p>

      <a id="How_to_change_computer_descriptions" name="How_to_change_computer_descriptions">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to change computer descriptions
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Samba_Server_for_files.2Ffolders_sharing_service" title="">
         #How to install Samba Server for files/folders sharing service
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       cp /etc/samba/smb.conf /etc/samba/smb.conf_backup
gedit /etc/samba/smb.conf
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Find this line
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       ...
  server string = Samba Server
...
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Replace with the following line
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       server string = new_computer_descriptions
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       testparm
/etc/init.d/smb restart
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_change_computer_Domain.2FWorkgroup" name="How_to_change_computer_Domain.2FWorkgroup">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to change computer Domain/Workgroup
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Samba_Server_for_files.2Ffolders_sharing_service" title="">
         #How to install Samba Server for files/folders sharing service
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       cp /etc/samba/smb.conf /etc/samba/smb.conf_backup
gedit /etc/samba/smb.conf
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Find this line
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       ...
  workgroup = MSHOME
...
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Replace with the following line
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       workgroup = new_domain_or_workgroup
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       testparm
/etc/init.d/smb restart
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_assign_Hostname_to_local_machine_with_dynamic_IP_using_free_DynDNS_service" name="How_to_assign_Hostname_to_local_machine_with_dynamic_IP_using_free_DynDNS_service">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to assign Hostname to local machine with dynamic IP using free DynDNS service
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that internet connections have been configured properly
         <br/>
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Register free Dynamic DNS at
         <a class="external free" href="https://www.dyndns.org" title="https://www.dyndns.org">
          https://www.dyndns.org
         </a>
         <br/>
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Automatically refresh IP in DynDNS Database/DNS every hour
         <br/>
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         * * * * * means minute hour date month year
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       yum -y install ipcheck
gedit /root/dyndns_update.sh
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines into the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       USERNAME=myusername
PASSWORD=mypassword
HOSTNAME=myhostname.dyndns.org
      </pre>
      <pre>
       cd /root/
if [ -f /root/ipcheck.dat ]; then
 ipcheck -r checkip.dyndns.org:8245 $USERNAME $PASSWORD $HOSTNAME
else
 ipcheck --makedat -r checkip.dyndns.org:8245 $USERNAME $PASSWORD $HOSTNAME
fi
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       chmod 700 /root/dyndns_update.sh
sh /root/dyndns_update.sh
export EDITOR=gedit &amp;&amp; crontab -e
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Append the following line at the end of file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       00 * * * * sh /root/dyndns_update.sh
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_share_folders_the_easy_way" name="How_to_share_folders_the_easy_way">

      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to access network folders without mounting
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">

        </a>

      <a id="How_to_mount.2Funmount_network_folders_manually.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read" name="How_to_mount.2Funmount_network_folders_manually.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to mount/unmount network folders manually, and allow all users to read
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Samba_Server_for_files.2Ffolders_sharing_service" title="">
         #How to install Samba Server for files/folders sharing service
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that network connections have been configured properly
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's IP: 192.168.0.1
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's Username: myusername
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's Password: mypassword
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Shared folder's name: linux
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Local mount folder: /media/sharename
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To mount network folder
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       mkdir /media/sharename
mount //192.168.0.1/linux /media/sharename/ -o username=myusername,password=mypassword
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To unmount network folder
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       umount /media/sharename/
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_mount.2Funmount_network_folders_manually.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read.2Fwrite" name="How_to_mount.2Funmount_network_folders_manually.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read.2Fwrite">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to mount/unmount network folders manually, and allow all users to read/write
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Samba_Server_for_files.2Ffolders_sharing_service" title="">
         #How to install Samba Server for files/folders sharing service
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that network connections have been configured properly
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's IP: 192.168.0.1
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's Username: myusername
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's Password: mypassword
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Shared folder's name: linux
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Local mount folder: /media/sharename
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To mount network folder
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       mkdir /media/sharename
mount //192.168.0.1/linux /media/sharename/ -o username=myusername,password=mypassword,dmask=777,fmask=777
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To unmount network folder
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       umount /media/sharename/
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_mount_network_folders_on_boot-up.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read" name="How_to_mount_network_folders_on_boot-up.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to mount network folders on boot-up, and allow all users to read
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_install_Samba_Server_for_files.2Ffolders_sharing_service" title="">
         #How to install Samba Server for files/folders sharing service
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that network connections have been configured properly
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's IP: 192.168.0.1
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's Username: myusername
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's Password: mypassword
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Shared folder's name: linux
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Local mount folder: /media/sharename
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       mkdir /media/sharename
gedit /root/.smbcredentials
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines into the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       username=myusername
password=mypassword
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       chmod 700 /root/.smbcredentials
cp /etc/fstab /etc/fstab_backup
gedit /etc/fstab
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Append the following line at the end of file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       //192.168.0.1/linux    /media/sharename cifs  credentials=/root/.smbcredentials    0    0
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_remount_.2Fetc.2Ffstab_without_rebooting" title="">
         #How to remount /etc/fstab without rebooting
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_mount_network_folders_on_boot-up.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read.2Fwrite" name="How_to_mount_network_folders_on_boot-up.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read.2Fwrite">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to mount network folders on boot-up, and allow all users to read/write
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>

         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>

        <a href="#How_to_install_Samba_Server_for_files.2Ffolders_sharing_service" title="">
         #How to install Samba Server for files/folders sharing service
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that network connections have been configured properly
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's IP: 192.168.0.1
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's Username: myusername
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Network computer's Password: mypassword
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Shared folder's name: linux
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Local mount folder: /media/sharename
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       mkdir /media/sharename
gedit /root/.smbcredentials
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Insert the following lines into the new file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       username=myusername
password=mypassword
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       chmod 700 /root/.smbcredentials
cp /etc/fstab /etc/fstab_backup
gedit /etc/fstab
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Append the following line at the end of file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       //192.168.0.1/linux    /media/sharename cifs  credentials=/root/.smbcredentials,dmask=0777,fmask=0777  0    0
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Save the edited file
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_remount_.2Fetc.2Ffstab_without_rebooting" title="">

        </a>
       </li>

      <a id="Remote_Desktop" name="Remote_Desktop">
      </a>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Remote Desktop
       </span>
      </h2>
      <a id="How_to_configure_remote_desktop_.28not_secure.29" name="How_to_configure_remote_desktop_.28not_secure.29">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to configure remote desktop (not secure)
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Warning! Remote Desktop will only work if there's a GNOME login session
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Leaving computer with an unattended GNOME login session is not secure
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Use (System -&gt; Lock Screen) and off the monitor when computer is left unattended
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Desktop -&gt; Preferences -&gt; Remote Desktop
       </li>
       <li>
        Remote Desktop Preferences
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       Sharing -&gt;
Allow other users to view your desktop (
       <b>
        Checked
       </b>
       )
Allow other users to control your desktop (
       <b>
        Checked
       </b>
       )
      </pre>
      <pre>
       Security -&gt;
Ask you for confirmation (Un-Checked)
Require the user to enter this password: (
       <b>
        Checked
       </b>
       )
Password: Specify the password
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_connect_into_remote_Fedora_desktop" name="How_to_connect_into_remote_Fedora_desktop">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to connect into remote Fedora desktop
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that remote Fedora machine have configured Remote Desktop
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Read
         <a href="#How_to_configure_remote_desktop_.28not_secure.29" title="">
          #How to configure remote desktop (not secure)
         </a>
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Remote Fedora machine: 192.168.0.1
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       vncviewer -fullscreen 192.168.0.1:0
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To quit vncviewer
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       Press 'F8' -&gt; Quit viewer
      </pre>
      <a id="Remote_conection_Script_by_fedorajim" name="Remote_conection_Script_by_fedorajim">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Remote conection Script by fedorajim
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Open a teminal window and switch to root.
      </p>
      <pre>
       gedit /usr/local/bin/remote2someone
      </pre>
      <p>
       Add the following text to the text editor
      </p>
      <pre>
       #!/bin/bash 
# Written by fedorajim 
# enter the IP address ofthe remote PC 
IPADDRESS="$(zenity --entry --title "Enter IP Address" --text "Enter the IP Address of the remore PC:")"
echo $IPADDRESS
#Enter the username you aregoing to login with 
UserName="$(zenity --entry --title "Enter User  Name" --text "Enter the User Name to connect with:")"
echo $UserName
# opens a new terminal window and connects to remote PC
function ssh_Remote_PC
{
gnome-terminal -x ssh -L 5911:$IPADDRESS:5901 $UserName@$IPADDRESS
}
function View_Remote_PC
{
gnome-terminal -x vncviewer localhost:11
}
#################################################
selection=
until [ "$selection" = "0" ]; do
echo ""
echo "######################"
echo "1 - Make Remote Connection"
echo "2 - display Remote Desktop"
echo "0 - exit program"
echo ""
echo -n "Enter selection: "
read selection
echo ""
#####################
# Commands executed #
#####################
case $selection in
1 ) $(ssh_Remote_PC);;
2 ) $(View_Remote_PC);;
0 ) exit;;
* ) echo "Please enter 1, 2  or 0"
esac
done
      </pre>
      <p>
       Click save and close the text editor.  Right click the desktop an choose create launcher 
add the following to the Create Launcher dialog
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Name: remote2someone
       </li>
       <li>
        Comment: ssh remote connection
       </li>
       <li>
        Command:  /usr/local/bin/remote2someone
       </li>
       <li>
        Type: application
       </li>
       <li>
        Run in Terminal: Checked
       </li>
       <li>
        Icon: click the Icon button and choose a icon
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       <br/>
       Click save.
      </p>
      <a id="How_to_connect_into_remote_Fedora_desktop_via_Windows_machine" name="How_to_connect_into_remote_Fedora_desktop_via_Windows_machine">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        Windows
       </span>
      </h2>
      <a id="How_to_install_support_for_NTFS" name="How_to_install_support_for_NTFS">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to install support for NTFS
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_add_extra_repositories" title="">
         #How to add extra repositories
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       yum -y install kernel-module-ntfs-$(uname -r)
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        For more info see
        <a class="external free" href="http://www.linux-ntfs.org" title="http://www.linux-ntfs.org">
         http://www.linux-ntfs.org
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <a id="How_to_mount.2Funmount_Windows_partitions_.28NTFS.29_manually.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read_only" name="How_to_mount.2Funmount_Windows_partitions_.28NTFS.29_manually.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read_only">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to mount/unmount Windows partitions (NTFS) manually, and allow all users to read only
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_list_partition_tables" title="">
         #How to list partition tables
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       <br/>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that /dev/hda1 is the location of Windows partition (NTFS)
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Local mount folder: /media/windows
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To mount Windows partition
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       mkdir /media/windows
mount /dev/hda1 /media/windows/ -t ntfs -o nls=utf8,umask=0222
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To unmount Windows partition
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       umount /media/windows/
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_mount.2Funmount_Windows_partitions_.28FAT.29_manually.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read.2Fwrite" name="How_to_mount.2Funmount_Windows_partitions_.28FAT.29_manually.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read.2Fwrite">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to mount/unmount Windows partitions (FAT) manually, and allow all users to read/write
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_list_partition_tables" title="">
         #How to list partition tables
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that /dev/hda1 is the location of Windows partition (FAT)
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Local mount folder: /media/windows
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To mount Windows partition
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       mkdir /media/windows
mount /dev/hda1 /media/windows/ -t vfat -o iocharset=utf8,umask=000
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        To unmount Windows partition
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       umount /media/windows/
      </pre>
      <a id="How_to_mount_Windows_partitions_.28NTFS.29_on_boot-up.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read_only" name="How_to_mount_Windows_partitions_.28NTFS.29_on_boot-up.2C_and_allow_all_users_to_read_only">
      </a>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline">
        How to mount Windows partitions (NTFS) on boot-up, and allow all users to read only
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#General_Notes" title="">
         #General Notes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Read
        <a href="#How_to_list_partition_tables" title="">
         #How to list partition tables
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         e.g. Assumed that /dev/hda1 is the location of Windows partition (NTFS)
        </i>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         Local mount folder: /media/windows
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <pre>
       mkdir /media/windows
cp /etc/fstab /etc/fstab_backup
gedit /etc/fstab
      </pre>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Append the following line at the end of file
       </li>
      </ul>
      <pre>
       /dev/hda1    /media/windows ntfs  nls=utf8,umask=0222 0    0
      </pre>
